1601 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Application of Kenning


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


72 Misc. 2d 929; 339 N.Y.S.2d 793; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1271



December 14, 1972 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners taxpayers instituted a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 78 for an order prohibiting respondent Department of Taxation and Finance (Department) from filing a tax warrant or levying against the petitioners for tax deficiencies for two years, claiming they were entitled to the relief because the Department failed to notify them of the tax deficiency and because certain sections of the Tax Law were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Department submitted records which indicated that a notice of deficiency for each of the tax years involved was mailed to the taxpayers by certified mail. The taxpayers alleged they never received the notices. The court held that under N.Y. Tax Law § 681(a) notice was only to be mailed by certified or registered mail to the taxpayer at his last known address, and the failure to receive the notice was immaterial. The court declared that N.Y. Tax Law §§ 612(f), 615(b)(2) were constitutional as the enactment of those sections served as an administrative convenience and presumably resulted in reducing expenses in the administration of the Department of Taxation and Finance. The state could properly classify taxpayers to promote administrative convenience and reduce expenses in the collection or measurement of income taxes.


OUTCOME: The disputed sections of the New York Tax Law were declared constitutional and the stay was continued for a period of 30 days within which time the taxpayers could institute an appeal and apply for a further stay to the appropriate court.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Taxation -- income tax -- notice of deficiency of income tax was mailed in compliance with statute; immaterial that it was not received -- issues challenging constitutionality of sections of Tax Law treated as though made in action for declaratory judgment -- husband earned all income but it was split; section 612 of Tax Law forbids splitting; section is constitutional -- section 615 of Tax Law which permits deductions to be taken by either spouse does not deny equal protection of law and is constitutional.

1. The mailing by the Department of Taxation and Finance of a notice of deficiency of income tax by certified mail complied with subdivision (a) of section 681 of the Tax Law and it is immaterial that petitioners failed to receive it.

2. Issues challenging the constitutionality of sections of the Tax Law are treated as though they were raised in an action for declaratory judgment. There is no requirement that administrative remedies be exhausted where the constitutionality of a statute is questioned.

3. Petitioners are husband and wife, the husband having earned all the income. For the tax years involved, the husband split his income with his wife, thereby reducing his [***2] tax liability. Respondent sent notices of deficiency claiming additional taxes due because under subdivision (f) of section 612 of the Tax Law a husband and wife may not split income. That subdivision provides that "If husband and wife determine their federal income tax on a joint return but determine their New York income taxes separately, they shall determine their New York adjusted gross income separately as if their federal adjusted gross incomes had been determined separately". Such subdivision is not unconstitutional and does not violate section 22 of article III of the Constitution which permitted the Legislature in any law imposing a tax on income to define income by reference to the laws of the United States as they may be in effect from time to time, with such exceptions or modifications as the Legislature may prescribe. The Legislature therefore was free to depart from the Federal law in its discretion and the prohibition against income splitting in subdivision (f) of section 612 of the Tax Law does not violate the Constitution.

4. Section 615 (subd. [b], par. [2]) of the Tax Law provides that "The total of the New York itemized deductions of a husband and wife [***3] whose federal taxable income is determined on a joint return, but whose New York taxable incomes are determined separately, may be taken by either or divided between them as they may elect." Such section is not unconstitutional as denying petitioners equal protection of the law. A tax inequality between classifications of taxpayers does not deny equal protection of the law since the classification rests upon a rational basis. The State may properly classify taxpayers to promote administrative convenience and reduce expenses in the collection or measurement of income taxes.

 

1602 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Acquisition of Real Prop.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Schenectady County


72 Misc. 2d 134; 338 N.Y.S.2d 730; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1272



December 13, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motions of respondent to dismiss the petitions, made at the close of the trial, are granted with appropriate exceptions to petitioners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city filed motions to dismiss petitioner landowners' petitions to vacate assessments related to the widening and grading of a public road. The landowners claimed that the assessments were unconstitutional and arbitrary and that they were improperly charged with land acquisition costs. The landowners had filed objections with the assessor, who adhered to his determination.


OVERVIEW: The common council properly adopted an ordinance authorizing the improvement of a public road and apportioning and assessing the cost of the improvement in proportion to the benefits derived. The ordinance set up a district to be assessed with the cost, however some lots outside the district derived a benefit from the improvement. The city engineer determined the itemized costs of the improvement, including the costs of overhead chargeable to the city and those to be assessed against the landowners, and the assessor published notice pursuant to Schenectady, N.Y. City Charter art. III, § 47. The assessor apportioned the assessments according to his determination of the benefit derived by each parcel, with those abutting the street receiving larger assessments than those more removed from it. The court granted the city's motion to dismiss, finding that the assessor had not engaged in fraud and that the landowners had not overcome the presumption of regularity of the proceedings in which the assessments had been determined.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motion to dismiss the landowners' actions to vacate assessments relating to the widening and grading of a public road.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- apportionment of cost of improvement -- sections of Schenectady City Charter which authorize street improvements and assess cost among owners in proportion to amount of benefit are constitutional -- charter was not violated; Assessor properly apportioned expense among properties benefited -- no benefited property was exempted from assessment -- charging land acquisition to district rather than whole city was proper -- Assessor followed general rule in assessing expense among benefited properties.

1. Sections of the Schenectady City Charter which authorize it to improve streets and assess the expense among the owners of land benefited in proportion to the amount of benefit are constitutional. The charter provided for the giving of notice to property owners and a full public hearing upon all the questions involved in assessments for local improvements. The ordinance implementing the charter is also constitutional.

2. The charter was not violated. It imposes the duty on the City Engineer to certify, from [***2] his records, to the Assessor the total amount to be assessed, itemized to the extent necessary to give the cost and expense of the work, labor and services performed, and materials furnished with the incidental costs. The Assessor also properly apportioned the expenses among the properties benefited by the improvement.

3. No property in the district benefited was exempted from the assessment. If any property beyond the ambit thereof was in any way benefited, a line had to be drawn somewhere and the Common council drew that line and its decision is conclusive, and not subject to review by the courts.

4. Charging the land acquisition expense to the district rather than to the whole city was proper.

5. The expense chargeable to the district was properly apportioned by the Assessor in accordance with his judgment as to the benefits received by the properties. The general rule for determining the amount of benefit is to ascertain the market value of each parcel with the improvement and without it. The excess of the one over the other is the amount of benefit. There is no evidence of market values with or without the improvements. Apportionment by determining that properties abutting [***3] the widened street would have the greatest enhancement of value, and that values would diminish further away was within the rule.

 

1603 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Aranofsky v. Grupposo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, Trial Term, New York County


72 Misc. 2d 701; 339 N.Y.S.2d 299; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1298



December 6, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment is therefore granted to the plaintiff for the relief demanded in the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff automobile owner instituted an action to recover an automobile in the custody of defendant Police Property Clerk of the City of New York.


OVERVIEW: The owner's automobile was seized after the owner's father was arrested for the illegal possession of untaxed cigarettes contained in the automobile. The owner was not named as a defendant, was not charged with any criminal activity. It was not alleged that the owners was in anyway involved in, or had any actual knowledge of the criminal use being made of the automobile by her father. At issue was whether the automobile was contraband and subject to forfeiture, despite its owner's noninvolvement in the alleged crime. The court held that the seizure of property not belonging to a defendant in a criminal action, without proof that the owner of the property was in fact a party to the criminal act, or knew and sanctioned the use of the property for criminal purposes, could not be permitted. The court directed the Property Clerk to turn over the automobile to the owner.


OUTCOME: The court granted the owner the relief demanded in her complaint.


HEADNOTES

Forfeitures and penalties -- property seized by police -- plaintiff's father was driving her car and was arrested for possessing untaxed cartons of cigarettes; District Attorney has executed release to plaintiff of her car; court directs Police Department Property Clerk to give her her car (Administrative Code of City of New York, § 435-4.0, subd. f; Tax Law, § 477-a).

Plaintiff's father was arrested for possessing 200 untaxed cartons of cigarettes. The cigarettes were in plaintiff's automobile. Plaintiff let her father use her automobile, but not for the purpose. The police seized the cigarettes and the automobile; but the District Attorney has executed a release of the automobile to plaintiff, since he does not need it as evidence, and since plaintiff is not charged with the crime. The case against her father is still pending. No forfeiture proceeding has ever been commenced against plaintiff (cf. Tax Law, § 477-a). There is no proof that plaintiff was involved in the possession of the untaxed cigarettes (cf. Administrative Code of City of New York, § 435-4.0, subd. f).  [***2] Under these circumstances, a summary seizure and forfeiture of plaintiff's property would violate due process of law. The Police Department Property Clerk is directed to turn over to plaintiff her automobile and her registration documents.

 

1604 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Woodside Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Gallman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


73 Misc. 2d 357; 341 N.Y.S.2d 757; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1322



November 30, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is granted to the extent of directing entry of judgment containing declarations favorable to the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff savings and loan association filed a motion for an order striking out the answers of defendant, the New York State Tax Commission, and directing entry of summary judgment with declarations favorable to the association. The association sought a declaration that certain city and state tax statutes were unconstitutional. The Commission requested entry of a declaratory judgment in its favor.


OVERVIEW: In the class action, the association contended that N.Y. Tax Law, art. 9-B, § 219-q(3) and New York City, N.Y., R. tit. 46, § 12.0, which imposed an alternative minimum tax upon savings banks and savings and loan associations, were violative of the New York and United States Constitutions upon the ground that such statutes differed from similar statutes affecting commercial banks. The association further claimed that the statutes constituted an ad valorem tax on intangible property contrary to constitutional prohibition and that such statutes denied the associations the equal protection of the law. The objections primarily related to the imposition on savings banks of a franchise tax under an alternative minimum tax formula not applied to other financial and banking institutions. The court held that the classifying of various bank institutions differently for legislative and tax purposes had a proper basis. The tax, as claimed, was not an ad valorem tax on intangible property proscribed by N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 3, nor was it a tax in violation of N.Y. Const. art. III, § 22. Accordingly, a judgment was entered in favor of the Commission.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Commission's motion to the extent of directing entry of judgment containing declarations favorable to the Commission.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- tax on savings institutions -- Tax Law ( § 219-q, subd. 3) and Administrative Code of City of New York (§ R46-12.0) imposing alternative minimum tax upon savings banks are constitutional -- distinction between savings and commercial banks justifies not imposing formula on commercial banks -- tax did not increase burden of savings banks -- tax is not ad valorem tax -- taxes comply with Constitution (art. III, § 22).

1. Subdivision 3 of section 219-q of article 9-B of the Tax Law and section R46-12.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York, which impose an alternative minimum tax upon savings banks and loan associations are constitutional.

2. Since there is a distinction between commercial and savings banks, the imposition of a minimum tax pursuant to a formula not applied to commercial banks is proper.

3. The alternative minimum tax did not increase but decreased the tax burden of savings banks by authorizing deduction of interest paid to depositors or interest payable if it were credited to depositors in computing the franchise [***2] tax. In addition, in its application the alternative tax is applied to dividends paid not in excess of 2% instead of on the total dividend paid out when in excess of 2%.

4. The tax is not an ad valorem tax on intangible property proscribed by section 3 of article XVI of the Constitution. Measurement of tax by percentage of interest or dividend is not an evaluation of property and assets owned.

5. The tax complies with section 22 of article III of the Constitution. The tax imposed is a franchise tax. What the tax is and upon whom imposed are clearly stated. The proceeds go into the general fund for public purposes.

 

1605 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stievater


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Erie County


77 Misc. 2d 761; 356 N.Y.S.2d 915; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1191



November 29, 1972, (Revised Opinion)


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Revision by Judge Bayger of his opinion dated August 24, 1972 which was published in 71 Misc 2d 29. On this revised opinion, the order of the County Court was reinstated by the Court of Appeals on June 6, 1974 (34 N Y 2d 793, modfg. 41 A D 2d 435).



DISPOSITION: The defendants' motion is granted and this indictment dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant architectural firms charged by plaintiff state with conspiracy and bribery in relation to construction of a sports stadium moved for dismissal on the grounds that they had received immunity under 18 U.S.C.S. § 2514.


OVERVIEW: Before plaintiff state charged defendant architectural firms with conspiracy and bribery related to construction of a sports stadium, there was a grand jury investigation into the matter. A similar inquiry had been previously commenced by federal authorities, which ultimately led to the grant of transactional immunity to defendants under 18 U.S.C.S. § 2514. Thus, when plaintiff state filed charges, defendants moved for dismissal on the basis of that grant of immunity, which they alleged was binding on both state and federal government. Plaintiff state agreed that its indictments referred to the same matters and transactions in issue in the federal proceeding, but it contended that there was no immunity as they neither used defendants' federal testimony, nor derived any leads from them, nor gained any benefit from such testimony. The court ruled for defendants and dismissed the indictments. It held that § 2514 itself was a constitutional exercise of Congressional power and that it precluded state as well as federal prosecution of an immunized witness for any crime to which his testimony referred. Thus, defendants' motion to dismiss was granted.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant architectural firms' motion to dismiss charges against them on the grounds that their grant of immunity in the federal proceeding relating to the same matters extended to state proceedings as well.


HEADNOTES

Witnesses -- immunity -- indictment of persons who, on account of same "transaction, matter or thing" had been granted full transactional immunity by Federal authorities under United States Code (tit. 18, § 2514), is dismissed.

The United States Code (tit. 18, § 2514), validly and constitutionally provides that, whenever in the judgment of a United States Attorney the testimony of any witness is needed before a Federal grand jury or Federal court, such United States Attorney, upon the approval of the United States Attorney General, shall request the Federal court to instruct the witness to testify despite self incrimination; and further, that, after giving such testimony, "No such witness shall be prosecuted * * * for or on account of any transaction, matter or thing concerning which he is [thus] compelled * * * to testify * * * nor shall testimony so [***2] compelled be used as evidence in any criminal proceeding * * * against him in any court." Even though such grant of full transactional immunity may be broader than is constitutionally necessary to eliminate the witness' privilege against self incrimination, such full grant of immunity is constitutionally binding upon the State courts, under the supremacy clause of the United States Constitution. Accordingly, the State court dismisses this State indictment of these witnesses, since this indictment covers the same "transaction, matter or thing concerning which" these defendants were compelled to testify before a Federal grand jury.

 

1606 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kokich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


District Court of New York, First District, Suffolk County


72 Misc. 2d 124; 338 N.Y.S.2d 463; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1327



November 29, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant's motion is, in all respects, denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought to suppress evidence for lack of adversary hearing or judicial scrutiny before his arrest, and to dismiss the complaint against him on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional, and the information failed to set forth a crime or sufficient facts to establish probable cause.


OVERVIEW: An undercover detective bought books and a film in a bookstore allegedly managed by defendant. The detective then made an information charging defendant with the crime of obscenity, second degree, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 235.05. The police returned to the bookstore and arrested defendant pursuant to an arrest warrant. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence, arguing an adversary proceeding was needed on the issue of obscenity before a valid arrest warrant could be issued. The court dismissed this contention. Although defendant cited authority stating that a hearing was required prior to issuance of a search warrant, defendant was challenging the issuance of an arrest warrant. The court also denied defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint. The obscenity statute, N.Y. Penal Law § 235.05, was not unconstitutional, and did not amount to dissimilar treatment of those similarly situated. The information was sufficient because it met the requirements of N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 100.40 and informed defendant of the nature of the charge against him.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motions to suppress evidence and dismiss the complaint against him were denied because the arrest warrant was valid, the statute was not unconstitutional, and the information was sufficient.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- informations -- detective purchased books and film in defendant's store; he then laid information charging defendant with obscenity and obtained arrest warrant; motion to suppress evidence is denied; no prior adversary hearing is required -- Penal Law ( § 235.05) is not unconstitutional -- information is proper in all respects -- whether material is obscene is question for trial.

1. A detective purchased two books and a film in the store managed by defendant. He then laid an information charging defendant with obscenity in the second degree (Penal Law, § 235.05, subd. 1) upon the basis of which an arrest warrant was issued. An adversary hearing or judicial scrutiny of the alleged obscene materials prior to defendant's arrest was not required. Defendant's motion to suppress the evidence is denied.

2. Section 235.05 of the Penal Law does not violate the Equal Protection Clause and is not unconstitutional.

3. The information properly describes the court and is correctly titled; it designates the offense charged, and the factual part contains nonhearsay allegations tending to support the charge and providing [***2] reasonable cause to believe that defendant committed the crime. The allegations, if true, establish the elements of the crime. The motion to dismiss the information is denied.

4. Whether or not the material is obscene is a question for trial.

 

1607 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Mobil Oil Corp. v. Huntington


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


72 Misc. 2d 530; 339 N.Y.S.2d 139; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1332



November 28, 1972 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oil company brought an action against defendants, a town and the State of New York, and sought a declaration that a town ordinance concerning oil spillage was constitutionally invalid. The oil company filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The oil company ran a marine oil terminal in the town. An ordinance required a permit from the town's oil spillage control board. There was a fee to obtain a permit. The ordinance also required that fees be paid according to the amount of oil transferred. These fees, up to a specified amount, went into the board's special fund to cover cleaning costs in the event of oil spillage. The court denied the summary judgment motion. N.Y. Town Law § 130(15), N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 10, and N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 2(c), para. 10 allowed the town to use its police powers to protect its lands and waters from oil spills. No preemption by the State Water Pollution Control Act, N.Y. Pub. Health Law §1200 et seq., or the Environmental Conservation Law, was alleged. The ordinance did not unconstitutionally infringe on federal maritime and admiralty jurisdiction because the special fund was targeted at "users" of harbor facilities rather than maritime shipping. There was no undue burden on interstate commerce because vessels were not excluded from the town's harbors and vessels were allowed to pass freely if they met minimum safety standards aimed at protecting the town's waters and lands.


OUTCOME: The court denied the oil company's summary judgment motion.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Health -- water pollution -- local Oil Spillage Control Board -- town ordinance apparently constitutionally requires any person or corporation engaged in unloading oil from ship to shore within town to obtain permit and give advance notice and pay fee into special fund maintained by town's Oil Spillage Control Board for purpose of cleaning town waters and uplands damaged by oil spills -- summary judgment of unconstitutionality denied.

An ordinance of the Town of Huntington (on Long Island) apparently validly and constitutionally requires any person or corporation engaged in unloading fuel oil and petroleum products in excess of 600 gallons from a vessel to shore within the town to pay for and obtain a permit from the town's Oil Spillage Control Board and to give advance notification of unloading; and, if transferring oil to an on-shore distribution depot, to pay one mill for every five gallons of oil transferred, into a special fund maintained by said Oil Spillage Control Board for the purpose of cleaning town waters and uplands damaged by oil spills, which fund is not to exceed $ 100,000. (N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 2, subd. [c], par. [10]; Town Law, § 130, subd. 15;  [***2] Municipal Home Rule Law, § 10.) The State of New York has intervened in this action and has specifically stated that it does not claim preemption by virtue of the State's Environmental Conservation Law or the State Water Pollution Control Act (Public Health Law, § 1200 et seq.). The Federal Water Pollution Control Act (U. S. Code, tit. 33, § 1151 et seq.) specifically disclaims against Federal preemption. This ordinance does not unduly burden interstate commerce. Nor does the ordinance infringe upon Federal admiralty and maritime jurisdiction (U. S. Const., art. III, § 2). Plaintiff oil corporation's motion for summary judgment of unconstitutionality is denied.

 

1608 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Da Grossa v. Goodman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


72 Misc. 2d 806; 339 N.Y.S.2d 502; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1337



November 27, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, petitioner's application is granted to the extent only of declaring that an interpretation of section 702 which denies to petitioner the right to file an application for a certificate of relief from disabilities is unconstitutional in that such interpretation would deny him equal protection of the law under section 11 of article I of the New York State Constitution. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner probationer, in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding in the nature of mandamus, sought a judgment directing respondent county clerk to accept for processing an application for a certificate of relief from civil disabilities or in the alternative declaring N.Y. Correct. Law § 702 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The probationer was convicted in a federal court for possessing stolen chattels. After his sentence was suspended, he was placed on probation. The refusal by the county clerk to accept his application allegedly violated due process of law under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV. N.Y. Correct. Law art. 23 was at issue, specifically N.Y. Correct. Law § 702(1). It was clear that the probationer was seeking to be relieved from disabilities that flowed under state law from his federal conviction. Further, if the probationer had been similarly convicted in the state courts his application would have been entertained. The county clerk argued that § 702 was only applicable to state court convictions. Such contention ran counter to the intended purpose that the legislature sought to achieve. The court granted the application in part, finding that an interpretation of § 702 was violative of N.Y. Const. art. 8, § 11, denying the probationer equal protection of the law. There was no rational basis or compelling state interest that justified the granting of the right to a state court convict but denied such right to a federal court convict.


OUTCOME: The probationer's application was granted in part to the extent of declaring that a statutory interpretation, which denied a right to file an application for a certificate of relief from disabilities, was unconstitutional, denying the probationer equal protection of the law. The county clerk was directed to accept and process such application in the same manner in which it would have been processed if it were a state court conviction.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- forfeitures and penalties -- convicted first offenders may apply to "court of this state" for relief from automatic forfeitures and disabilities (Correction Law, art. 23, § 702); convicted Federal first offenders may likewise apply to our State court (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 11).

The Correction Law (art. 23, § 702, subd. 1) provides that a "court of this state may, in its discretion, issue a certificate of relief from disabilities to an eligible [first] offender for a conviction that occurred such court", etc. This must be construed to apply to a conviction which occurred in a Federal court, since, otherwise, our statute would deny the equal protection of the laws (N. Y. Const., art. I., § 11).

 

1609 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Piesco v. Di Francesca


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Rockland County


72 Misc. 2d 128; 338 N.Y.S.2d 286; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1346



November 21, 1972 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought an action against defendants, individuals and Board of Trustees of the Village of Piermont, seeking a declaration of the invalidity of a zoning ordinance affecting their waterfront properties. The landowners asserted that the ordinance was unconstitutional and deprived them of unlimited use of the waters of the Hudson River and appurtenant uplands. The case went to trial.


OVERVIEW: The landowners initiated an action against defendants seeking a declaration that a zoning ordinance was invalid to the extent that it affected their waterfront properties. After a trial, the trial court rendered judgment, holding as to the first and second cause of action that there was no showing by either party justifying any declaratory relief as to the issues of confiscatory taking of property or unconstitutional discrimination in the application of the ordinance. The trial court entered a declaratory judgment as to the third and fourth causes of action, which alleged that the ordinance was an unconstitutional deprivation of use of the river waters and appurtenant uplands. It held that although the zoning ordinance was invalid insofar as it operated to preclude the proper exercise by landowners of their riparian rights, the causes of action sought solely a declaration of invalidity of the use restrictions on their upland lots, not a decree declaring their riparian rights. Thus, the trial court declared that the landowners, bound by the use restrictions imposed on their upland lots, could not utilize riparian rights to expand the permitted uses for such lots.


OUTCOME: The trial court entered declaratory relief upholding the zoning ordinance as against the landowners on their causes of action alleging unconstitutional deprivation of land. The trial court dismissed the causes of action asserting confiscatory taking and discriminatory application of the ordinance.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- village zoning ordinance placed plaintiffs' riverfront properties in W-2 district for which no use as of right was provided; permits for use as marina docks, etc. were authorized; plaintiffs' present use was continued as nonconforming use; plaintiffs have failed to prove that ordinance is confiscatory as to their properties -- cause of action that ordinance is discriminatory has not been shown -- ordinance is invalid insofar as it deprives plaintiffs of their riparian rights and insofar as it regulates waterfront by individual lot use by special permit.

1. A village zoning ordinance placed plaintiffs' riverfront lots in a W-2 district. The ordinance provided no use as of right for lands in such district but did provide for the issuance of special permits for marinas, docks and other river uses. The areas of plaintiffs' lots do not comply with the minimum bulk regulations of the ordinance and the lots therefore do not qualify for a special permit for any of the permitted uses. The ordinance authorizes the continuance of any lawful use of building or land existing at the time of the enactment of the ordinance even though nonconforming. In [***2] this action for a declaration that the ordinance is unconstitutional the gravamen of the first cause is that the restriction imposed on plaintiffs' lots precludes use of said property for any purpose to which it is reasonably adapted. Plaintiffs made no factual showing permitting a determination of whether they have suffered any significant economic injury. It does not appear whether or not the properties were practicably and profitably used in accordance with the authorized nonconforming use provisions of the ordinance. The record is not such that declaratory relief may be awarded with respect to the claim that the ordinance is confiscatory or invalid as imposing unreasonable restrictions on the beneficial uses of plaintiffs' properties materially affecting their values.

2. The second cause of action alleges that the ordinance is discriminatory and denies equal protection of the law. Such cause has not been established. There was no showing that the zoning was not in accordance with a reasonable and comprehensive plan, nor does it appear that the resulting dissimilarity in authorized nonconforming uses of the zoned property was other than merely incidental to proper planning.

 [***3] 3. The third and fourth causes of action charge that the ordinance deprives plaintiffs of unlimited use of the waters of the Hudson River appurtenant and adjacent to their uplands, and that the power to regulate uses of water rests solely with the State. The ordinance is invalid insofar as it restricts the otherwise lawful use of lands under the river. Insofar as it places lands under water in a restricted district, the ordinance may not be sustained as one adopted pursuant to the power vested in a village by section 46-a of the Navigation Law to regulate use of vessels in waters within or bounding said village. Moreover, this statute does not authorize regulation lot by lot by the use of the special permit procedures in a zoning ordinance. Although the zoning ordinance is invalid insofar as it may operate to preclude the proper exercise by plaintiffs of their riparian rights, plaintiffs' causes of action seek solely a declaration of invalidity of the use restrictions on their upland lots rather than a decree protecting or declaring their riparian rights. In any event, plaintiffs, bound by the use restrictions imposed on their upland lots, may not utilize riparian rights to expand [***4] the permitted uses for such lots. Furthermore, there is no claim or factual showing by the plaintiffs of any interference with such rights as are authorized by law including the statutes and regulations of the United States and of the State of New York and of proper governmental agencies. Also the exercise of such rights would be subject to the proper regulation by the village under aforesaid section 46-a of the Navigation Law.

 

1610 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Franklin v. Krause


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Nassau County


72 Misc. 2d 104; 338 N.Y.S.2d 561; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2350



November 16, 1972 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents brought an action to have the court appoint a nonpartisan commission to prepare a plan of apportionment. The residents had previously been granted a judgment declaring that defendant county board of supervisors was illegally apportioned and ordering the board to adopt a valid plan within six months after public announcement of the enumeration of the inhabitants of the county.


OVERVIEW: The litigants disputed the starting date of that six-month period and the residents contended that the plan adopted by the board was only a warmed over version of the one previously held unconstitutional. The court concluded that the plan adopted was clearly a strained attempt to keep the old unconstitutional apportionment, tailored here and there to fit the mandated minimal requirements. However, the court held that the board still failed to meet the requirements. The court reasoned that weighted voting could have been approved solely as a temporary expedient; but that a permanent plan must have been based on the principle of one man, one vote. The court reasoned that the board improperly divided some of the votes evenly between two supervisors and the other votes very unevenly among the other four supervisors. The court held that this prevented these legislators from individually and substantially having the same influence as the others. The court ordered the board to submit a new plan within 60 days, holding that from the standpoint of ordinary votes, from the standpoint of voting power, and from the standpoint of weighted voting, the plan did not comply with the requirements.


OUTCOME: The court denied the resident's application for an order appointing a nonpartisan commission to prepare and submit to the court a plan of apportionment and voting.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- apportionment of Board of Supervisors -- weighted voting plan for Nassau County Board of Supervisors disapproved as unconstitutional.

A proposed weighted voting plan for the apportionment of the Board of Supervisors of Nassau County (Local Laws, 1972, No. 13 of Nassau County) is disapproved by Trial Term as unconstitutional and as failing to meet the directions of the Court of Appeals (26 N Y 2d 65).

 

1611 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Krstovich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Greene County


72 Misc. 2d 90; 338 N.Y.S.2d 132; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1392



November 6, 1972 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for an order dismissing an indictment returned against him by the grand jury, superseding the district attorney, and remanding his case to a local criminal court other than the local criminal court in the jurisdiction in which the alleged crime took place on the ground that the district attorney who filed the charges had a personal interest in the case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with misdemeanor criminal mischief under N.Y. Penal Law § 145.00. The damaged premises were owned by the district attorney of the county. Defendant alleged the district attorney was disqualified from prosecuting his case because of personal interest, and filed a motion to dismiss the indictment, supersede the district attorney, and remand the case to a criminal court in a different jurisdiction. The court found the record disclosed legally sufficient evidence for the indictment, but held that the indictment should have been dismissed. Under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 170.20, 170.25, defendant was placed under the burden of making a motion to a superior court and showing good cause while the district attorney was not required to give notice or show cause to anyone when deciding where a misdemeanor complaint should have been prosecuted. The court therefore held the statutes resulted in unfair and discriminatory results and violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV even if they were not facially invalid. The court dismissed the indictment as void because an interested party, the district attorney, was in the grand jury room, and found the district attorney was disqualified.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the indictment, superseded the district attorney, remanded the case with instructions that a change of venue be granted, and appointed a special district attorney for the prosecution of the case because the district attorney who filed the charges had a personal interest in the case.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- prosecution by indictment -- CPL 170.20, which enables prosecutor to prosecute misdemeanor charge by indictment by merely requesting adjournment, whereas defendant is required to make motion on notice and on showing of good cause, is unconstitutional -- District Attorney, as owner of premises allegedly damaged, is disqualified from prosecuting charge of criminal mischief against defendant -- indictment is vacated -- court removes prosecution to town Justice Court.

1. CPL 170.20 provides for removal of a prosecution from a local criminal court by the District Attorney with a request for an adjournment without a motion and without notice to anyone and the section makes mandatory the grant of an adjournment so that the District Attorney may proceed by indictment. CPL 170.25 providing for removal of a prosecution from a local criminal court at defendant's instance requires that he make a motion upon notice to the District Attorney showing good cause for prosecution by indictment. CPL 170.20 unconstitutionally lends itself to unequal application of the law in its operation and delays the speedy trial of lesser crimes. The grant of the District Attorney's application [***2] here for adjournment of the charge of criminal mischief in the fourth degree (Penal Law, § 145.00) in a village Justice Court was unconstitutional.

2. Morever, the premises allegedly damaged by the alleged criminal mischief were owned by the District Attorney. Had he been obliged to apply to the County Court for removal of the case to the Grand Jury, his interest would have been disclosed. He is disqualified for interest in the prosecution against defendant.

3. His disqualification requires that the indictment be set aside. His disqualification prohibited his presence in the Grand Jury room under CPL 190.25 (subd. 3) as a person not authorized.

4. The court on its own initiative removes the prosecution from the village Justice Court of the village wherein the District Attorney lives, has his private law practice and where he has clients, to a Justice Court of a town. The District Attorney is superseded by a special District Attorney specially appointed for the prosecution of this case.

 

1612 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ungar v. New York City Comm'n on Human Rights


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


71 Misc. 2d 1048; 337 N.Y.S.2d 629; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1397



November 6, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the defendant's motion for summary judgment is granted and plaintiffs' motion for a stay denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff general partner brought an action against defendant New York City Commission on Human Rights for a judgment declaring unconstitutional the provisions of the New York City Administrative Code creating the defendant New York City Commission on Human Rights, Administrative Code of City of New York, § B1-1.0 et seq. By companion motion, plaintiffs moved for an order staying discovery.


OVERVIEW: The commission initiated proceedings against plaintiffs charging that plaintiffs had utilized discriminatory practices in renting apartments. Plaintiffs alleged that the applicable statutes did not authorize the issuance of a complaint unless it was founded upon the report of an aggrieved party, not the commission's investigator, that he had been the victim of actual discrimination in housing. The court held that it would not hold the commission powerless to act absent a third-party complaint. Such a holding would severely restrict the performance of its function, which was the elimination of discrimination as a wrong to all, not merely to a single offended person. The courts had passed the stage in implementation of constitutional rights where the proper government function was considered solely that of arbiter and enforcer of these rights when denied to specific persons. Affirmative action in implementation was now recognized virtually everywhere as a proper government function. The court need decide only that such affirmative action may properly be taken and that the administrative agency's interpretation of the enabling legislation that grants it that power is reasonable.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion for summary judgment was granted and plaintiffs' motion for a stay was denied.


HEADNOTES

Civil rights -- discrimination in housing -- City Commission on Human Rights has power to initiate investigation of discrimination without third-party complaint -- no triable issue raised by claim of discrimination in enforcement -- joinder of accusatory and judgment functions in defendant commission is not unlawful -- no entrapment of plaintiffs occurred.

1. Under the provisions of the Administrative Code of City of New York which created defendant Commission on Human Rights (§ B1-1.0 et seq.), it was granted power to initiate its own investigation of discrimination and to file complaints alleging violations. Thus, defendant commission can act even in the absence of a complaint by a third party.

2. No triable issue is raised by plaintiffs as to claimed discrimination in enforcement because they are the first to have been proceeded against.

3. The joinder of the accusatory and judgment functions in the commission is not unlawful or unconstitutional.

4. The discriminatory design here, if ultimately established, did not originate within the commission, whose [***2] agents afforded plaintiffs an opportunity to violate the anti-discrimination laws. This is not entrapment.

 

1613 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Goldstein v. Urstadt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


74 Misc. 2d 540; 344 N.Y.S.2d 774; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1415



October 30, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, since the actions of the respondent can in no manner be characterized as arbitrary, capricious or illegal, the petition is denied in all respects and dismissed.

Settle judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent commissioner of housing (commissioner) removed petitioner tenants from their positions as board members of a housing company. The tenants brought an article 78 proceeding seeking an order or judgment determining that the action of the commissioner was unconstitutional, illegal, arbitrary, and capricious.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner sent instructions to the tenants to perform a statutorily required annual income review of the tenants in the housing units for purposes of determining the propriety of a rental increase. After the tenants ignored several requests to perform the review, they were removed as board members and replaced with housing department employees. The tenants asserted that the removal procedures were illegal, unconstitutional, arbitrary, and capricious and that pursuant to N.Y. Priv. Hous. Fin. Law § 13, subd. 15, if the commissioner was of the opinion that the directors had failed or omitted to do an act required by law or by the commissioner, in order to compel compliance the commissioner was required to institute an action in the supreme court. The court dismissed the tenants' petition, finding that the commissioner was not required to commence an action or proceeding to compel compliance with his orders, or the statutory mandates, but such resort was only one remedy available to the commissioner.


OUTCOME: The tenants' petition seeking to have the actions of the commissioner declared illegal, unconstitutional, arbitrary, and capricious was denied and dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- limited-profit housing -- State Commissioner of Housing and Community Renewal may remove and replace directors of limited-profit housing company who refuse to require tenants to submit to annual review of their income (Private Housing Finance Law, § 13, subd. 15) -- this power of Commissioner constitutionally applies even to companies previously incorporated.

1. The Commissioner of the Division of Housing and Community Renewal of the State of New York has the power to remove and replace the board of directors of a limited-profit housing company because of their refusal to require the tenants to submit to an annual review of their income (Private Housing Finance Law, § 13, subd. 15; § 31). The Commissioner need not first bring an action or proceeding (cf. Private Housing Finance Law, § 32, subd. 7).

2. Although this power of the Commissioner was added to the incorporation statute (Private Housing Finance Law, § 13, subd. 15) some years after this limited-profit [***2] housing company was incorporated, this provision of the incorporation applies retroactively (N. Y. Const., art. X, § 1; Business Corporation Law, § 110).

People v. Simmons


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, New York County


71 Misc. 2d 940; 337 N.Y.S.2d 717; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1420



October 30, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the transfer of his case by the trial court to the Centralized Special Narcotics Parts in New York County (New York) on the ground that the establishment of special courts for drug-related crimes by N.Y. Jud. Law §§ 177-a to 177-e was unconstitutional in that it deprived him of due process of law and equal protection of law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for criminal possession of a dangerous drug and after several trial court appearances, his case was transferred to a special narcotics court, which had been created by the state legislature. Defendant filed a motion challenging the transfer of his case and claimed the statute that created the special courts, N.Y. Jud. Law §§ 177-a to 177-e, was unconstitutional in that it deprived him of due process and equal protection of law. The court stated the statute was passed in response to a crisis in drug enforcement in large cities because their already strained criminal justice systems could not handle the ever-increasing caseload. The court held there was a strong presumption in favor of the constitutionality of a legislative enactment and that defendant bore the burden of establishing invalidity beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant had presented no evidence to support his allegations of discrimination in selecting the cases to be sent to the specialized court or of the imposition of more severe sentences by the specialized court. The court therefore held the statute was constitutional and denied defendant's motion.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion challenging the constitutionality of the statute which created the specialized courts for drug-related cases because defendant failed to meet his burden of establishing the invalidity of the statute beyond a reasonable doubt.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Special Narcotics Parts -- centralized Special Narcotics Parts of Supreme Court, New York County, are constitutional (Judiciary Law, art. 5-B).

The emergency Special Narcotics Parts of the Supreme Court (Judiciary Law, art. 5-B, § 177-a et seq.) which have been centralized in New York County are constitutional.

 

1615 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Wenner v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


71 Misc. 2d 978; 337 N.Y.S.2d 733; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1421



October 30, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The complaint is dismissed without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a judicial declaration that N.Y. Educ. Law § 3621 required defendant school district to provide bus transportation to his children, who attended a parochial school 17 miles from his home. The school argued that § 3621(1)(b) imposed a 10-mile limit upon parochial school busing.


OVERVIEW: The father demanded transportation for his children pursuant to § 3621(3)(c), which stated that the district was not obligated to transport parochial school students except to the "nearest available" parochial school. The father asserted that the 10-mile limit imposed by § 3621(1)(b) did not apply to transportation provided under § 3621(3)(c). He also argued that § 3621 was unconstitutionally arbitrary and discriminatory because it improperly discriminated between students. In dismissing his complaint, the court held the language of § 3621(3)(c) merely modified the district's § 3621(1)(b)transportation obligations. Section 3621(3)(c) gave the district the right to deny public transportation to any student who wished to attend a more distant, rather than a closer, parochial school; it did not operate to remove the 10-mile limit otherwise imposed upon parochial school busing. Section § 3621 was not unconstitutional merely because it provided different transportation assistance to different classes of pupils; the State was not required to provide the same degree of busing to parochial school pupils that it provided to public school students.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the father's complaint without an award of costs.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- transportation of pupils -- school district is not required to transport plaintiff's children to parochial school located more than 10 miles away (Education Law, § 3621).

Subdivision 1 of section 3621 of the Education Law requires each school district to provide transportation to and from schools legally attended for "b. Non-public school pupils residing within the districts who * * * live a distance of more than two miles and up to ten miles from such school." Subdivision 3 provides: "This section shall not be deemed to require * * * c. A school district to provide transportation for a pupil attending a parochial school of his denomination except to and from the nearest available parochial school of such denomination". Under these provisions defendant school district is not required to transport five of plaintiff's children to the nearest parochial school located 17 miles from his home. The 10-mile limitation in paragraph b of subdivision 1 cannot be disregarded because of the language of paragraph c of subdivision 3. The latter paragraph modifies the former rather than renders the former meaningless.

 

1616 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Dalton v. Van Dien


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Orange County


72 Misc. 2d 287; 339 N.Y.S.2d 378; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1426



October 27, 1972 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 72 Misc. 2d 292 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a mobile home owner, instituted a declaratory judgment action against defendants, Town of Warwick and a building inspector, seeking a determination that the mobile home maintained on the owner's property was not in violation of a zoning ordinance or, in the alternative, for a determination that the zoning ordinance was unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: After he was convicted of permitting a trailer to be maintained on his property in violation of a zoning ordinance, the owner filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the town's enforcement of the ordinance. Rejecting the owner's claim that that there was a distinction between mobile homes and trailers and that only the latter were prohibited by the ordinance, the court ruled that the evidence established that the mobile home was a "trailer" as defined by the ordinance. The court also ruled that an invalidly issued building permit did not create an estoppel against enforcement of the ordinance. Noting that the Town took no action against trailers installed prior to 1966 on the ground that they were non-conforming uses, the court determined that trailers that were in violation of the zoning ordinance both before and after 1966 could not acquire non-conforming status, that the Town's policy of enforcing its ordinance only against trailers placed after 1966 was arbitrary and unreasonable and, being based on an unjustifiable standard, the Town's enforcement policy amounted to discriminatory treatment proscribed by the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court entered a judgment declaring that the zoning ordinance, to the extent that it prohibited the owner from maintaining a mobile home on his property, was unenforceable.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- prior conviction for violation of town's zoning ordinance does not bar action for declaration that plaintiff's mobile home is not in violation thereof -- ordinance applies to mobile home which is trailer within ordinance -- issuance of building permit for erection of trailer does not estop municipality -- evidence shows that town does not prosecute violators who erected trailers before 1966; prosecution against those erecting trailers after 1966 is arbitrary; plaintiff entitled to declaration that his trailer is not in violation.

1. Plaintiff's prior criminal conviction for violating a town's zoning ordinance by maintaining a trailer on his property is not a bar to an action for a judgment declaring that his mobile home is not a violation of the zoning ordinance.

2. While a distinction does exist between a mobile home and a house trailer, the ordinance applies. Plaintiff's mobile home is a trailer within the definition of the ordinance.

3. Plaintiff, before purchasing the property, erecting the mobile home on a foundation and installing a septic tank, obtained a building permit. The issuance of the building permit [***2] does not estop the municipality from enforcing its zoning laws.

4. Although the zoning ordinance forbade trailers in residential districts as early as 1962, mobile homes erected prior to 1966 were not proceeded against, the building inspector testifying that it was town policy to proceed against trailers erected after 1966. Trailers which were in violation of the town's ordinance both before and after the 1966 amendment could not acquire nonconforming status. The town's policy of enforcing restrictions against post 1966 trailers is arbitrary and unreasonable and entitles plaintiff to the declaration he seeks.

 

1617 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Utica v. Mercon, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Oneida County


71 Misc. 2d 680; 336 N.Y.S.2d 880; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1429



October 26, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition for a preliminary injunction must be denied and the temporary stay vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the City of Utica, filed an action for a permanent injunction against defendant trading stamp company.. The City moved pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 63 to obtain a preliminary restraining order against the company.


OVERVIEW: The company was licensed by the state to do business under the provisions of Article 29-E of the New York General Business Law. The company solicited distributors to distribute stamps to various households in the state. The City had a hawkers and peddlers ordinance. The company did not obtain any licensing under the City's ordinance. The City commenced an action against the company in order to permanently enjoin the company from engaging in its business activities. The City then moved pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 63 to preliminarily restrain or enjoin the company. The company contended that its activities were not subject to the ordinance, or, if they were, that the ordinance was unconstitutional. Ultimately, the court denied the City's motion for the preliminary injunction. The court held that the state law under which the company was registered regulated trading stamp companies; thus, the company could not be subject to the City's ordinance because state law had already preempted the field that the City was attempting to regulate, making the City's ordinance invalid.


OUTCOME: The court denied the City's motion for the preliminary injunction and vacated a temporary stay.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- regulation of trading stamp companies -- State has preempted regulation of trading stamp companies (General Business Law, art. 29-E) and city cannot enforce hawkers and peddlers ordinance against such company -- contention not contained in complaint, cannot be entertained.

1. By section 578 of article 29-E of the General Business Law, which provides that "the regulation of trading stamp companies * * * shall be governed solely by the provisions of this article and no local laws or ordinances shall be promulgated with respect thereto", the State has preempted this subject and plaintiff city cannot enforce against defendant, a foreign trading stamp company, licensed to do business under article 29-E, an ordinance requiring hawkers and peddlers to obtain a license because defendant's distributors go from door to door leaving empty stampbooks and telling each householder which businesses give stamps. Such ordinance is invalid. The city's motion for a preliminary injunction is denied.

2. A contention based on an affidavit by one of defendant's distributors that [***2] defendant should be restrained because its sale of distributorships is, in effect, the sale of securities, since not contained in the complaint, cannot be entertained.

 

1618 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Block


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


71 Misc. 2d 714; 337 N.Y.S.2d 153; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1430



October 26, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Based on the foregoing, the court finds the defendant Stewart guilty on all three counts of the indictment and the defendant Block not guilty on the first count but guilty under the second and third counts of the indictment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their convictions in the trial court (New York) for three counts of promoting prostitution in the second degree in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 230.25(1), 230.25(2), and two counts of promoting prostitution in the second degree in violation of § 230.25(2), respectively. Defendants challenged the constitutionality of the statutes and the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, one and two, were indicted for three counts of promoting prostitution in the second degree in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 230.25(1), 230.25(2), and at the end of trial defendant one was convicted on all three counts and defendant two was convicted on two counts of violating § 230.25(2). Defendants appealed the judgments of conviction. The court held U.S. Const. only required that the language of a statute convey sufficiently definite warning as to the proscribed conduct when measured by common understanding and practices. Because the same word or group of words used in different parts of the same statute were presumed to have the same meaning, the court held that §§ 230.25(1), (2) were not vague when the terms "sexual conduct" and "fee" were sufficiently precise in various other sections of N.Y. Penal Law. The court further held that under N.Y. Penal Law §§ 230.35, 230.15, defendants could not be convicted solely by the uncorroborated testimony of the prostitutes on which their crimes were based, and every element of the crimes charged had to be corroborated. Accordingly, judgments of conviction against defendants were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgments of conviction against defendants were affirmed because statutes conveyed sufficiently definite warning as to the proscribed conduct when the terms "sexual conduct" and "fee" were precisely defined in various other sections of the New York Penal Law and because every element of crimes charged was adequately corroborated.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- prostitution -- employers of females in massage parlors guilty of promoting prostitution; statute constitutional.

The employers of females who, for a fee, massaged and manipulated the private parts of male customers to a climax, were found guilty of promoting prostitution in the second degree (Penal Law, § 230.25, subds. 1, 2; § 230.00; cf. Penal Law, § 5.00; § 130.00 subds. 2, 3; § 235.20, subd. 3). The statute is constitutional, and every material element of the crimes was proved and corroborated (Penal Law, § 230.35; cf. § 130.15).

 

1619 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Grossman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, New York County


71 Misc. 2d 1050; 337 N.Y.S.2d 712; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1436



October 25, 1972 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner executors brought an action under Surr. Ct. Proc. Act § 1421 to determine the validity and effect of an election by respondent, decedent's surviving spouse. The executors contended that pursuant to N.Y. Est. Powers & Trusts Law § 5-1.1(c)(1) inter vivos dispositions to the widow were properly includible in the estate of the decedent for the purpose of computing the widow's share and were the dispositions to be offset against her share.


OVERVIEW: The decedent executed a will on February 25, 1965, which had been admitted to probate. The decedent was unmarried at the time of execution. He married respondent, his surviving spouse, on October 10, 1967. Subsequent to that marriage decedent made certain inter vivos dispositions to the surviving spouse. The issue presented was whether the inter vivos dispositions to the widow were properly includible in the estate of the decedent for the purpose of computing the widow's share and were dispositions for the benefit of the widow to be offset against her share as computed. The court held that the statute and the intent of the legislature were clear. If the will was executed on or before August 31, 1966, no inter vivos transaction before or after that date was a testamentary substitute. It was not the date of marriage that mattered, but the date of the execution of the will. The court would not, under the guise of interpreting N.Y. Est. Powers & Trusts Law § 5-1.1(c)(1), read into the statute an exception which was not present therein. Unless all three conditions set forth in the statute were present the inter vivos transfers were exempt transactions and not testamentary substitutes.


OUTCOME: The court held that the inter vivos transfers from the decedent to the surviving spouse were exempt transactions, and that the surviving spouse was entitled to take her share against the assets passing under decedent's will. The computation of her elective share was not to include the testamentary substitutes specified by the executors, nor could they be set off against her share as computed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Wills -- election to take intestate share -- since decedent's will was executed before August 31, 1966 and he married after that date, inter vivos dispositions to widow who has elected against will, may not be included in computation of intestate share nor may they be set off against said share.

Testator executed his will on February 25, 1965 while unmarried and thereafter married respondent on October 10, 1967 to whom he made inter vivos dispositions. EPTL 5-1.1 gives a surviving spouse a right of election and it includes testamentary substitutes if (1) the will was executed after August 31, 1966; (2) the transactions were effected during the marriage; and (3) the transactions were effected after August 31, 1966. Conditions (2) and (3) are met here but not condition (1). There is no express or implied requirement in the statute that the surviving spouse must have been married to decedent at the time the will was executed. Under the statute, if the will was executed on or before August 31, 1966, no inter vivos transaction before or after that date is a testamentary substitute. Respondent surviving wife is entitled to elect to take her share against the assets passing [***2] under decedent's will, excluding from the computation of her elective share the inter vivos dispositions. Such dispositions may not be set off against her share as computed.

New York Standardbred Farm Owners, Inc. v. Agriculture & New York State Horse Breeding Development Fund


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


71 Misc. 2d 671; 336 N.Y.S.2d 825; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1444



October 20, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The relief requested by plaintiffs is denied except as to the request concerning the running of a minimum of 12 races at each track. With regard to the latter the relief is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners' association brought a declaratory judgment action to set aside certain of defendant state horse breeding fund's rules and to enjoin the fund from proceeding according to those rules.


OVERVIEW: The owners brought an action to set aside the fund's rules whereby a horse's eligibility for a stakes race was based on the number of points it had accumulated. The points were accumulated by finishing first, second, third, or fourth in certain preliminary races. The court noted that the legislature directed the fund to provide for stake events conditioned to admit only horses dropped from a mare bred in New York. It did not make every horse bred in conformance with the statutory requisites eligible. Thus, the fund's rulemaking power was not limited to establishing a system whereby it could obtain information concerning the age, gait and parentage of a horse. The fund was allowed to limit the eligibility of horses, and it did not exceed its statutory authority when it created the point qualification system. The point qualification system was consistent with the overall statutory plan, which was not only to improve horse breeding but to support state and local governments with pari-mutuel betting revenue. The fund did exceed its authority by running less than 12 races at a particular harness track.


OUTCOME: The court denied the owners' relief except as to the request to require the running of a minimum of 12 races at each track.


HEADNOTES

Horse racing -- harness races -- Agriculture and New York State Horse Breeding Development Fund validly limits eligibility for final races of Sire Stakes to horses which have accumulated points at previous races.

The Agriculture and New York State Horse Breeding Development Fund, a public benefit corporation, validly and properly limits eligibility for the final races of the Sire Stakes to harness horses which are bred in New York State and which accumulated points for first, second, third and fourth places at previous Sire Stake races; however, the Fund must run at least 12 such previous races at each track (L. 1965, ch. 567, as amd. [Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law, art. IV, § 99-e, subd. 2]).
